<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">History of technology</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="hatnote" role="note">This article is about the technology in human history. For the book series, see <a href="/wiki/History_of_Technology_(book_series)" title="History of Technology (book series)">History of Technology (book series)</a>. For the academic discipline that studies the history of technology, see <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology" title="History of science and technology">History of science and technology</a>. For an account of the contemporary use of production techniques, see <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">Technology</a>. For a historical account of economically important technologies, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Productivity_improving_technologies_(economic_history)" title="Productivity improving technologies (economic history)">Productivity improving technologies (economic history)</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Technology_(disambiguation)" title="Technology (disambiguation)">Technology (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ur_chariot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1356" data-file-width="2660" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ur_chariot.jpg/300px-Ur_chariot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ur_chariot.jpg/450px-Ur_chariot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ur_chariot.jpg/600px-Ur_chariot.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ur_chariot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">wheel</a>, invented sometime before the 4th millennium BC, is one of the most ubiquitous and important technologies. This detail of the "Standard of Ur", ca. 2500 BC., displays a Sumerian <a href="/wiki/Chariot" title="Chariot">chariot</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>history of technology</b> is the history of the <a href="/wiki/Invention" title="Invention">invention</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tool" title="Tool">tools</a> and techniques and is similar to other sides of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_history" title="Human history">history of humanity</a>. Technology can refer to methods ranging from as simple as <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stone_tools" title="Stone tools">stone tools</a> to the complex <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetic engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a> that has emerged since the 1980s.</p>
<p>New knowledge has enabled people to create new things, and conversely, many scientific endeavors are made possible by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technologies" title="Technologies">technologies</a> which assist humans in <a href="/wiki/Travel" title="Travel">travelling</a> to places they could not previously reach, and by <a href="/wiki/Scientific_instrument" title="Scientific instrument">scientific instruments</a> by which we study nature in more detail than our natural senses allow.</p>
<p>Since much of technology is <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied science</a>, technical history is connected to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science" title="History of science">history of science</a>. Since technology uses <a href="/wiki/Resource" title="Resource">resources</a>, technical history is tightly connected to <a href="/wiki/Economic_history" title="Economic history">economic history</a>. From those resources, technology produces other resources, including <i>technological artifacts</i> used in <a href="/wiki/Everyday_life" title="Everyday life">everyday life</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Technological_change" title="Technological change">Technological change</a> affects, and is affected by, a society's cultural <a href="/wiki/Tradition" title="Tradition">traditions</a>. It is a force for <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a> and a means to develop and project economic, political and military power.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measuring_technological_progress">Measuring technological progress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Measuring technological progress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociologists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropologists</a> have created <a href="/wiki/Social_theory" title="Social theory">social theories</a> dealing with <a href="/wiki/Social_evolution" title="Social evolution">social</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_evolution" title="Cultural evolution">cultural evolution</a>. Some, like <a href="/wiki/Lewis_H._Morgan" title="Lewis H. Morgan">Lewis H. Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leslie_White" title="Leslie White">Leslie White</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Lenski" title="Gerhard Lenski">Gerhard Lenski</a>, have declared <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technological_progress" title="Technological progress">technological progress</a> to be the primary factor driving the development of human civilization. Morgan's concept of three major stages of social evolution (savagery, <a href="/wiki/Primitive_culture" title="Primitive culture">barbarism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>) can be divided by technological milestones, such as <a href="/wiki/Fire" title="Fire">fire</a>. White argued the measure by which to judge the evolution of culture was <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>For White, "the primary function of <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>" is to "harness and control energy." White differentiates between five stages of <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" title="Human development (humanity)">human development</a>: In the first, people use energy of their own muscles. In the second, they use energy of <a href="/wiki/Domestication_of_animals" title="Domestication of animals">domesticated animals</a>. In the third, they use the energy of plants (<a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">agricultural revolution</a>). In the fourth, they learn to use the energy of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>: coal, oil, gas. In the fifth, they harness <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a>. White introduced a formula P=E*T, where E is a measure of energy consumed, and T is the measure of efficiency of technical factors utilizing the energy. In his own words, "culture evolves as the amount of energy harnessed per capita per year is increased, or as the efficiency of the instrumental means of putting the energy to work is increased". Russian astronomer <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Kardashev" title="Nikolai Kardashev">Nikolai Kardashev</a> extrapolated his theory, creating the <a href="/wiki/Kardashev_scale" title="Kardashev scale">Kardashev scale</a>, which categorizes the energy use of advanced civilizations.</p>
<p>Lenski's approach focuses on <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">information</a>. The more information and knowledge (especially allowing the shaping of <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">natural environment</a>) a given society has, the more advanced it is. He identifies four stages of human development, based on advances in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_communication" title="History of communication">history of communication</a>. In the first stage, information is passed by <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a>. In the second, when humans gain <a href="/wiki/Sentience" title="Sentience">sentience</a>, they can <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Learn" title="Learn">learn</a> and pass information through by experience. In the third, the humans start using signs and develop <a href="/wiki/Logic" title="Logic">logic</a>. In the fourth, they can create <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">symbols</a>, develop <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">writing</a>. Advancements in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communications_technology" title="Communications technology">communications technology</a> translates into advancements in the <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">economic system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_system" title="Political system">political system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Distribution_of_wealth" title="Distribution of wealth">distribution of wealth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">social inequality</a> and other spheres of social life. He also differentiates societies based on their level of technology, communication and economy:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a>,</li>
<li>simple <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a>,</li>
<li>advanced agricultural,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Industry" title="Industry">industrial</a>,</li>
<li>special (such as fishing societies).</li>
</ul>
<p>In economics <a href="/wiki/Productivity" title="Productivity">productivity</a> is a measure of technological progress. Productivity increases when fewer inputs (labor, energy, materials or land) are used in the production of a unit of output.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Another indicator of technological progress is the development of new products and services, which is necessary to offset unemployment that would otherwise result as labor inputs are reduced. In developed countries productivity growth has been slowing since the late 1970s; however, productivity growth was higher in some economic sectors, such as manufacturing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> For example, in employment in <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_in_the_United_States" title="Manufacturing in the United States">manufacturing in the United States</a> declined from over 30% in the 1940s to just over 10% 70 years later. Similar changes occurred in other developed countries. This stage is referred to as <i>post-industrial</i>.</p>
<p>In the late 1970s sociologists and anthropologists like <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Toffler" title="Alvin Toffler">Alvin Toffler</a> (author of <i><a href="/wiki/Future_Shock" title="Future Shock">Future Shock</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bell" title="Daniel Bell">Daniel Bell</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Naisbitt" title="John Naisbitt">John Naisbitt</a> have approached the theories of <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">post-industrial societies</a>, arguing that the current era of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_society" title="Industrial society">industrial society</a> is coming to an end, and <a href="/wiki/Service_(economics)" title="Service (economics)">services</a> and information are becoming more important than <a href="/wiki/Industry" title="Industry">industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Good_(economics)" title="Good (economics)">goods</a>. Some extreme visions of the post-industrial society, especially in <a href="/wiki/Fictional_technology" title="Fictional technology">fiction</a>, are strikingly similar to the visions of near and post-<a href="/wiki/Technological_singularity" title="Technological singularity">Singularity</a> societies.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="By_period_and_geography">By period and geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: By period and geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1400" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg/220px-Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg/330px-Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg/440px-Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Farming-on-Indonesia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> preceded <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">writing</a> in the history of technology.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The following is a summary of the history of technology by time period and geography:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olduvai_Gorge" title="Olduvai Gorge">Olduvai</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stone_technology" title="Stone technology">stone technology</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olduwan" title="Olduwan">Olduwan</a>) 2.5 million years ago (scrapers; to butcher dead animals)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Acheulean" title="Acheulean">Acheulean</a> stone technology 1.6 million years ago (hand axe)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fire" title="Fire">Fire</a> creation and manipulation, used since the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a>, possibly by <a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a> as early as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E13_s" title="1 E13 s">1.5 Million years ago</a></li>
<li>(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens sapiens">Homo sapiens sapiens</a> - modern human anatomy arises, around 200,000 years ago.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clothing" title="Clothing">Clothing</a> possibly 170,000 years ago.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">Stone tools</a>, used by <a href="/wiki/Homo_floresiensis" title="Homo floresiensis">Homo floresiensis</a>, possibly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_E12_s" title="1 E12 s">100,000 years ago</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">Ceramics</a> c. 25,000 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">Domestication</a> of animals, c. 15,000 BC</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bow_(weapon)" title="Bow (weapon)">Bow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sling_(weapon)" title="Sling (weapon)">sling</a> c. 9th millennium BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microlith" title="Microlith">Microliths</a> c. 9th millennium BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plough" title="Plough">Plough</a> c. 4000 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">Wheel</a> c. 4000 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gnomon" title="Gnomon">Gnomon</a> c. 4000 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">Writing systems</a> c. 3500 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">Copper</a> c. 3000 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">Bronze</a> c. 2500 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">Salt</a> c. 2500 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chariot" title="Chariot">Chariot</a> c. 2000 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">Iron</a> c. 1500 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sundial" title="Sundial">Sundial</a> c. 800 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">Glass</a> ca. 500 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Catapult" title="Catapult">Catapult</a> c. 400 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horseshoe" title="Horseshoe">Horseshoe</a> c. 300 BC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stirrup" title="Stirrup">Stirrup</a> first few centuries AD</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_technology" title="Prehistoric technology">Prehistoric technology</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stone_Age">Stone Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stone Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2468" data-file-width="3290" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg/220px-Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg/330px-Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg/440px-Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prehistoric_Tools_-_Les_Combarelles_-_Les_Eyzies_de_Tayac_-_MNP.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A variety of <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">stone tools</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During most of the <b><a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a></b> - the bulk of the Stone Age - all humans had a lifestyle which involved limited tools and few permanent settlements. The first major technologies were tied to survival, hunting, and food preparation. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stone_tools" title="Stone tools">Stone tools</a> and weapons, <a href="/wiki/Control_of_fire_by_early_humans" title="Control of fire by early humans">fire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_clothing_and_textiles" title="History of clothing and textiles">clothing</a> were technological developments of major importance during this period.</p>
<p>Human ancestors have been using stone and other tools since long before the emergence of <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> approximately 200,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The earliest methods of <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">stone tool</a> making, known as the <a href="/wiki/Oldowan" title="Oldowan">Oldowan</a> "industry", date back to at least 2.3 million years ago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> with the earliest direct evidence of tool usage found in <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley,_Kenya" title="Great Rift Valley, Kenya">Great Rift Valley</a>, dating back to 2.5 million years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> This era of stone tool use is called the <i><a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a></i>, or "Old stone age", and spans all of human history up to the development of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> approximately 12,000 years ago.</p>
<p>To make a stone tool, a "<a href="/wiki/Lithic_core" title="Lithic core">core</a>" of hard stone with specific flaking properties (such as <a href="/wiki/Flint" title="Flint">flint</a>) was struck with a <a href="/wiki/Hammerstone" title="Hammerstone">hammerstone</a>. This flaking produced sharp edges which could be used as tools, primarily in the form of <a href="/wiki/Chopper_(archaeology)" title="Chopper (archaeology)">choppers</a> or <a href="/wiki/Scraper_(archaeology)" title="Scraper (archaeology)">scrapers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ea_archaeology_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-ea_archaeology-7">[7]</a></sup> These tools greatly aided the early humans in their <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> lifestyle to perform a variety of tasks including <a href="/wiki/Butcher" title="Butcher">butchering</a> carcasses (and breaking bones to get at the <a href="/wiki/Bone_marrow" title="Bone marrow">marrow</a>); chopping wood; cracking open nuts; skinning an animal for its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hides" title="Hides">hide</a>; and even forming other tools out of softer materials such as bone and wood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The earliest stone tools were crude, being little more than a fractured rock. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acheulian" title="Acheulian">Acheulian</a> era, beginning approximately 1.65 million years ago, methods of working these stone into specific shapes, such as <a href="/wiki/Hand_axe" title="Hand axe">hand axes</a> emerged. This early Stone Age is described as <a href="/wiki/Epipaleolithic" title="Epipaleolithic">Epipaleolithic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a>. The former is generally used to describe the early Stone Age in areas with limited glacial impact.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a>, approximately 300,000 years ago, saw the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Prepared-core_technique" title="Prepared-core technique">prepared-core technique</a>, where multiple blades could be rapidly formed from a single core stone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ea_archaeology_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-ea_archaeology-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a>, beginning approximately 40,000 years ago, saw the introduction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pressure_flaking" title="Pressure flaking">pressure flaking</a>, where a wood, bone, or antler <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punch_(engineering)" title="Punch (engineering)">punch</a> could be used to shape a stone very finely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The later Stone Age, during which the rudiments of agricultural technology were developed, is called the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> period. During this period, polished <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">stone tools</a> were made from a variety of hard rocks such as <a href="/wiki/Flint" title="Flint">flint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jade" title="Jade">jade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jadeite" title="Jadeite">jadeite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenschist" title="Greenschist">greenstone</a>, largely by working exposures as quarries, but later the valuable rocks were pursued by tunnelling underground, the first steps in mining technology. The polished axes were used for forest clearance and the establishment of crop farming, and were so effective as to remain in use when bronze and iron appeared.</p>
<p>Stone Age cultures developed <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_music" title="Prehistoric music">music</a>, and engaged in organized <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_warfare" title="Prehistoric warfare">warfare</a>. Stone Age humans developed ocean-worthy <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">outrigger canoe</a> technology, leading to <a href="/wiki/History_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="History of Papua New Guinea">migration</a> across the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malay_archipelago" title="Malay archipelago">Malay archipelago</a>, across the Indian Ocean to <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> and also across the Pacific Ocean, which required knowledge of the ocean currents, weather patterns, sailing, and <a href="/wiki/Celestial_navigation" title="Celestial navigation">celestial navigation</a>.</p>
<p>Although Paleolithic cultures left no written records, the shift from nomadic life to settlement and agriculture can be inferred from a range of archaeological evidence. Such evidence includes ancient tools,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cave_painting" title="Cave painting">cave paintings</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_art" title="Prehistoric art">prehistoric art</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Willendorf" title="Venus of Willendorf">Venus of Willendorf</a>. Human remains also provide direct evidence, both through the examination of bones, and the study of <a href="/wiki/Mummy" title="Mummy">mummies</a>. Scientists and historians have been able to form significant inferences about the lifestyle and culture of various prehistoric peoples, and especially their technology.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Copper_and_bronze_Ages">Copper and bronze Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Copper and bronze Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sword_bronze_age_(2nd_version).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1000" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sword_bronze_age_%282nd_version%29.jpg/170px-Sword_bronze_age_%282nd_version%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sword_bronze_age_%282nd_version%29.jpg/255px-Sword_bronze_age_%282nd_version%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Sword_bronze_age_%282nd_version%29.jpg/340px-Sword_bronze_age_%282nd_version%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sword_bronze_age_(2nd_version).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A late <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_sword" title="Bronze Age sword">Bronze Age sword</a> or dagger blade</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Stone Age developed into the <b><a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a></b> after the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a>. The Neolithic Revolution involved radical changes in agricultural technology which included <a href="/wiki/History_of_agriculture" title="History of agriculture">development of agriculture</a>, animal <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestication</a>, and the adoption of permanent settlements. These combined factors made possible the development of metal <a href="/wiki/Smelting" title="Smelting">smelting</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a>, an alloy of <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a> and copper, being the materials of choice, although polished stone tools continued to be used for a considerable time owing to their abundance compared with the less common metals (especially tin).</p>
<p>This technological trend apparently began in the <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">Fertile Crescent</a>, and spread outward over time. These developments were not, and still are not, universal. The <a href="/wiki/Three-age_system" title="Three-age system">three-age system</a> does not accurately describe the technology history of groups outside of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, and does not apply at all in the case of some isolated populations, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spinifex_People" title="Spinifex People">Spinifex People</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sentinelese_people" title="Sentinelese people">Sentinelese</a>, and various Amazonian tribes, which still make use of Stone Age technology, and have not developed agricultural or metal technology.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Age">Iron Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Iron Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age,_found_at_Gotland,_Sweden.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="282" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age%2C_found_at_Gotland%2C_Sweden.jpg/130px-Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age%2C_found_at_Gotland%2C_Sweden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age%2C_found_at_Gotland%2C_Sweden.jpg/195px-Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age%2C_found_at_Gotland%2C_Sweden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age%2C_found_at_Gotland%2C_Sweden.jpg/260px-Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age%2C_found_at_Gotland%2C_Sweden.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Axe_of_iron_from_Swedish_Iron_Age,_found_at_Gotland,_Sweden.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/Axe" title="Axe">axehead</a> made of iron, dating from the Swedish <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_age" title="Iron age">Iron age</a></b> involved the adoption of iron <a href="/wiki/Bloomery" title="Bloomery">smelting</a> technology. It generally replaced bronze, and made it possible to produce tools which were stronger, lighter and cheaper to make than bronze equivalents. In many Eurasian cultures, the Iron Age was the last major step before the development of written language, though again this was not universally the case. It was not possible to mass manufacture steel because high furnace temperatures were needed, but <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> could be produced by <a href="/wiki/Forging" title="Forging">forging</a> bloomery iron to reduce the carbon content in a controllable way. Iron ores were much more widespread than either copper or tin. In Europe, large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hill_fort" title="Hill fort">hill forts</a> were built either as a refuge in time of war, or sometimes as permanent settlements. In some cases, existing forts from the Bronze Age were expanded and enlarged. The pace of land clearance using the more effective iron axes increased, providing more farmland to support the growing population.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_technology" title="Ancient technology">Ancient technology</a></div>
<p>It was the growth of the ancient civilizations which produced the greatest advances in technology and engineering, advances which stimulated other societies to adopt new ways of living and governance.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptians">Egyptians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Egyptians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptians</a> invented and used many simple machines, such as the <a href="/wiki/Inclined_plane" title="Inclined plane">ramp</a> to aid construction processes. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilization" title="Indus Valley Civilization">Indus Valley Civilization</a>, situated in a resource-rich area, is notable for its early application of city planning and sanitation technologies. Ancient India was also at the forefront of seafaring technology—a panel found at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohenjodaro" title="Mohenjodaro">Mohenjodaro</a> depicts a sailing craft. Indian construction and architecture, called '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vaastu_Shastra" title="Vaastu Shastra">Vaastu Shastra</a>', suggests a thorough understanding of materials engineering, hydrology, and sanitation.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mesopotamians">Mesopotamians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mesopotamians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The peoples of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumerians" title="Sumerians">Sumerians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrians" title="Assyrians">Assyrians</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonians" title="Babylonians">Babylonians</a>) have been credited with the invention of the <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">wheel</a>, but this is no longer certain. They lived in cities from c. 4000 BC,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and developed a sophisticated architecture in mud-brick and stone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> including the use of the true arch. The walls of Babylon were so massive they were quoted as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wonder_of_the_World" title="Wonder of the World">Wonder of the World</a>. They developed extensive water systems; canals for transport and irrigation in the alluvial south, and catchment systems stretching for tens of kilometres in the hilly north. Their palaces had sophisticated drainage systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dalley2013_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dalley2013-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Writing was invented in Mesopotamia, using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuneiform" title="Cuneiform">cuneiform</a> script. Many records on clay tablets and stone inscriptions have survived. These civilizations were early adopters of bronze technologies which they used for tools, weapons and monumental statuary. By 1200 BC they could cast objects 5 m long in a single piece. The Assyrian King <a href="/wiki/Sennacherib" title="Sennacherib">Sennacherib</a> (704-681 BC) claims to have invented automatic sluices and to have been the first to use water screws, of up to 30 tons weight, which were cast using two-part clay moulds rather than by the 'lost wax' process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dalley2013_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dalley2013-13">[13]</a></sup> The Jerwan Aqueduct (c. 688 BC) is made with stone arches and lined with waterproof concrete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_astronomical_diaries" title="Babylonian astronomical diaries">Babylonian astronomical diaries</a> spanned 800 years. They enabled meticulous astronomers to plot the motions of the planets and to predict eclipses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese">Chinese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Chinese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Chinese made many first-known discoveries and developments. Major technological contributions from China include early <a href="/wiki/Seismometer" title="Seismometer">seismological detectors</a>, matches, <a href="/wiki/Paper" title="Paper">paper</a>, sliding calipers, the double-action piston pump, <a href="/wiki/Cast_iron" title="Cast iron">cast iron</a>, the iron plough, the multi-tube <a href="/wiki/Seed_drill" title="Seed drill">seed drill</a>, the wheelbarrow, the <a href="/wiki/Suspension_bridge" title="Suspension bridge">suspension bridge</a>, the parachute, natural gas as fuel, the <a href="/wiki/Compass" title="Compass">compass</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Raised-relief_map" title="Raised-relief map">raised-relief map</a>, the propeller, the <a href="/wiki/Crossbow" title="Crossbow">crossbow</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Pointing_Chariot" title="South Pointing Chariot">South Pointing Chariot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a>.</p>
<p>Other Chinese discoveries and inventions from the Medieval period,include: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Block_printing" title="Block printing">block printing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Movable_type" title="Movable type">movable type printing</a>, phosphorescent paint, endless power <a href="/wiki/Chain_drive" title="Chain drive">chain drive</a> and the clock escapement mechanism. The solid-fuel <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rocket</a> was invented in China about 1150, nearly 200 years after the invention of <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a> (which acted as the rocket's fuel). Decades before the West's age of exploration, the Chinese emperors of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a> also sent <a href="/wiki/Treasure_voyages" title="Treasure voyages">large fleets</a> for maritime voyages, some reaching Africa.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek">Greek</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Greek">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeolipile_illustration.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="714" data-file-width="471" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Aeolipile_illustration.png/170px-Aeolipile_illustration.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Aeolipile_illustration.png/255px-Aeolipile_illustration.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Aeolipile_illustration.png/340px-Aeolipile_illustration.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeolipile_illustration.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An illustration of the <a href="/wiki/Aeolipile" title="Aeolipile">aeolipile</a>, the earliest steam-powered device</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">Hellenistic</a> engineers <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_technology" title="Ancient Greek technology">were responsible for myriad inventions and improvements to existing technology</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a> in particular saw a sharp increase in technological advancement, fostered by a climate of openness to new ideas, the blossoming of a mechanistic philosophy, and the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Alexandria" title="Library of Alexandria">Library of Alexandria</a> and its close association with the adjacent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museion" title="Museion">museion</a>. In contrast to the typically anonymous inventors of earlier ages, ingenious minds such as <a href="/wiki/Archimedes" title="Archimedes">Archimedes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philo_of_Byzantium" title="Philo of Byzantium">Philo of Byzantium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_Alexandria" title="Hero of Alexandria">Heron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ctesibius" title="Ctesibius">Ctesibius</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Archytas" title="Archytas">Archytas</a> remain known by name to posterity.</p>
<p>Ancient Greek innovations were particularly pronounced in mechanical technology, including the ground-breaking invention of the <a href="/wiki/Watermill" title="Watermill">watermill</a> which constituted the first human-devised motive force not to rely on muscle power (besides the <a href="/wiki/Sail" title="Sail">sail</a>). Apart from their pioneering use of waterpower, Greek inventors were also the first to experiment with wind power (see <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_Alexandria" title="Hero of Alexandria">Heron</a>'s windwheel) and even created the earliest steam engine (the <a href="/wiki/Aeolipile" title="Aeolipile">aeolipile</a>), opening up entirely new possibilities in harnessing natural forces whose full potential would not be exploited until the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>. The newly devised right-angled <a href="/wiki/Gear" title="Gear">gear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Screw" title="Screw">screw</a> would become particularly important to the operation of mechanical devices. That is when the age of mechanical devices started.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="620" data-file-width="600" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg/220px-Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg/330px-Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg/440px-Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Overshot_water_wheel_schematic.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The compartmented water-wheel, here its overshot version, was invented in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">Hellenistic times</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ancient agriculture, as in any period prior to the modern age the primary mode of production and subsistence, and its irrigation methods, were considerably advanced by the invention and widespread application of a number of previously unknown water-lifting devices, such as the vertical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water-wheel" title="Water-wheel">water-wheel</a>, the compartmented wheel, the water <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">turbine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archimedes%27_screw" title="Archimedes' screw">Archimedes' screw</a>, the bucket-chain and pot-garland, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Force_pump" title="Force pump">force pump</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suction_pump" title="Suction pump">suction pump</a>, the double-action <a href="/wiki/Piston_pump" title="Piston pump">piston pump</a> and quite possibly the <a href="/wiki/Chain_pump" title="Chain pump">chain pump</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis_2000_356f._16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis_2000_356f.-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In music, the <a href="/wiki/Water_organ" title="Water organ">water organ</a>, invented by Ctesibius and subsequently improved, constituted the earliest instance of a <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">keyboard instrument</a>. In time-keeping, the introduction of the inflow <a href="/wiki/Water_clock" title="Water clock">clepsydra</a> and its mechanization by the dial and pointer, the application of a <a href="/wiki/Feedback" title="Feedback">feedback system</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Escapement" title="Escapement">escapement</a> mechanism far superseded the earlier outflow clepsydra.</p>
<p>The famous <a href="/wiki/Antikythera_mechanism" title="Antikythera mechanism">Antikythera mechanism</a>, a kind of analogous computer working with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Differential_gear" title="Differential gear">differential gear</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Astrolabe" title="Astrolabe">astrolabe</a> both show great refinement in astronomical science.</p>
<p>Greek engineers were also the first to devise <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automata" title="Automata">automata</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Vending_machine" title="Vending machine">vending machines</a>, suspended ink pots, automatic <a href="/wiki/Washstand" title="Washstand">washstands</a> and doors, primarily as toys, which however featured many new useful mechanisms such as the <a href="/wiki/Cam" title="Cam">cam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gimbal" title="Gimbal">gimbals</a>.</p>
<p>In other fields, ancient Greek inventions include the <a href="/wiki/Catapult" title="Catapult">catapult</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gastraphetes" title="Gastraphetes">gastraphetes</a> crossbow in warfare, hollow bronze-casting in metallurgy, the <a href="/wiki/Dioptra" title="Dioptra">dioptra</a> for surveying, in infrastructure the <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">lighthouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_heating" title="Central heating">central heating</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tunnel_of_Eupalinos" title="Tunnel of Eupalinos">tunnel excavated from both ends by scientific calculations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Diolkos" title="Diolkos">ship trackway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">dry dock</a> and plumbing. In horizontal vertical and transport great progress resulted from the invention of the <a href="/wiki/Crane_(machine)" title="Crane (machine)">crane</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Winch" title="Winch">winch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wheelbarrow" title="Wheelbarrow">wheelbarrow</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Odometer" title="Odometer">odometer</a>.</p>
<p>Further newly created techniques and items were <a href="/wiki/List_of_ancient_spiral_stairs" title="List of ancient spiral stairs">spiral staircases</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chain_drive" title="Chain drive">chain drive</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliper" title="Caliper">sliding calipers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shower" title="Shower">showers</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman">Roman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Roman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pont_du_gard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pont_du_gard.jpg/220px-Pont_du_gard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pont_du_gard.jpg/330px-Pont_du_gard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pont_du_gard.jpg/440px-Pont_du_gard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pont_du_gard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pont_du_Gard" title="Pont du Gard">Pont du Gard</a> in France, a Roman aqueduct</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> developed an intensive and sophisticated agriculture, expanded upon existing iron working technology, created <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">laws</a> providing for individual ownership, advanced stone masonry technology, advanced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_road" title="Roman road">road-building</a> (exceeded only in the 19th century), military engineering, civil engineering, spinning and weaving and several different machines like the <a href="/wiki/Reaper" title="Reaper">Gallic reaper</a> that helped to increase productivity in many sectors of the Roman economy. Roman engineers were the first to build monumental arches, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Roman_amphitheatres" title="List of Roman amphitheatres">amphitheatres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_aqueduct" title="Roman aqueduct">aqueducts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermae" title="Thermae">public baths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_bridge" title="Roman bridge">true arch bridges</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harbour" title="Harbour">harbours</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">reservoirs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dam" title="Dam">dams</a>, vaults and domes on a very large scale across their Empire. Notable Roman inventions include the <a href="/wiki/Codex" title="Codex">book (Codex)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glass_blowing" title="Glass blowing">glass blowing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">concrete</a>. Because Rome was located on a volcanic peninsula, with sand which contained suitable crystalline grains, the <a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">concrete</a> which the Romans formulated was especially durable. Some of their buildings have lasted 2000 years, to the present day.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inca_and_Mayan">Inca and Mayan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Inca and Mayan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The engineering skills of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inca" title="Inca">Inca</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayans" title="Mayans">Mayans</a> were great, even by today's standards. An example is the use of pieces weighing upwards of one ton in their stonework placed together so that not even a blade can fit in-between the cracks. The villages used irrigation canals and <a href="/wiki/Drainage" title="Drainage">drainage</a> systems, making agriculture very efficient. While some claim that the Incas were the first inventors of <a href="/wiki/Hydroponics" title="Hydroponics">hydroponics</a>, their agricultural technology was still soil based, if advanced. Though the <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya civilization</a> had no metallurgy or wheel technology, they developed complex writing and astrological systems, and created sculptural works in stone and flint. Like the Inca, the Maya also had command of fairly advanced agricultural and construction technology. Throughout this time period, much of this construction was made only by women, as men of the Maya civilization believed that females were responsible for the creation of new things. The main contribution of the <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztec</a> rule was a system of communications between the conquered cities. In <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>, without draft animals for transport (nor, as a result, wheeled vehicles), the roads were designed for travel on foot, just like the Inca and Mayan civilizations</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_to_early_modern">Medieval to early modern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Medieval to early modern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Asia">East Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: East Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_China" title="History of science and technology in China">History of science and technology in China</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_Korea" title="History of science and technology in Korea">History of science and technology in Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Japan" title="Science and technology in Japan">Science and technology in Japan</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_of_the_Song_dynasty" title="Science and technology of the Song dynasty">Science and technology of the Song dynasty</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_inventions" title="List of Chinese inventions">List of Chinese inventions</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Japanese_inventions" title="List of Japanese inventions">List of Japanese inventions</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indian_subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Indian subcontinent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="History of science and technology in the Indian subcontinent">History of science and technology in the Indian subcontinent</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_inventions_and_discoveries" title="List of Indian inventions and discoveries">List of Indian inventions and discoveries</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_world">Islamic world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Islamic world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_inventions_in_the_medieval_Islamic_world" title="List of inventions in the medieval Islamic world">List of inventions in the medieval Islamic world</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_Agricultural_Revolution" title="Arab Agricultural Revolution">Arab Agricultural Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Science_in_the_medieval_Islamic_world" title="Science in the medieval Islamic world">Science in the medieval Islamic world</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Iran" title="Science and technology in Iran">Science and technology in Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Science and technology in the Ottoman Empire">Science and technology in the Ottoman Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_contributions_to_Medieval_Europe" title="Islamic contributions to Medieval Europe">Islamic contributions to Medieval Europe</a></div>
<p>As earlier empires had done, the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">caliphates</a> united in trade large areas that had previously traded little. The conquered sometimes paid lower taxes than in their earlier independence, and ideas spread even more easily than goods. Peace was more frequent than it had been. These conditions fostered improvements in agriculture and other technology as well as in sciences which largely adapted from earlier Greek, Roman and Persian empires, with improvements.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Europe">Medieval Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Medieval Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trebuchet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Trebuchet.jpg/220px-Trebuchet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Trebuchet.jpg/330px-Trebuchet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Trebuchet.jpg/440px-Trebuchet.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trebuchet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Medieval <a href="/wiki/Trebuchet" title="Trebuchet">counterweight trebuchet</a> (reconstruction)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medieval_technology" title="Medieval technology">Medieval technology</a></div>
<p>European technology in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> may be best described as a symbiosis of <i>traditio et innovatio</i>. While medieval technology has been long depicted as a step backwards in the evolution of Western technology, sometimes willfully so by modern authors intent on denouncing the church as antagonistic to scientific progress (see e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myth_of_the_Flat_Earth" title="Myth of the Flat Earth">Myth of the Flat Earth</a>), a generation of medievalists around the American historian of science <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lynn_White" title="Lynn White">Lynn White</a> stressed from the 1940s onwards the innovative character of many medieval techniques. Genuine medieval contributions include for example <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanical_clock" title="Mechanical clock">mechanical clocks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spectacles" title="Spectacles">spectacles</a> and vertical <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmills</a>. Medieval ingenuity was also displayed in the invention of seemingly inconspicuous items like the <a href="/wiki/Watermark" title="Watermark">watermark</a> or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Push_button" title="Push button">functional button</a>. In navigation, the foundation to the subsequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_exploration" title="Age of exploration">age of exploration</a> was laid by the introduction of pintle-and-gudgeon <a href="/wiki/Rudder" title="Rudder">rudders</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lateen_sail" title="Lateen sail">lateen sails</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry_compass" title="Dry compass">dry compass</a>, the horseshoe and the <a href="/wiki/Astrolabe" title="Astrolabe">astrolabe</a>.</p>
<p>Significant advances were also made in military technology with the development of <a href="/wiki/Plate_armour" title="Plate armour">plate armour</a>, steel <a href="/wiki/Crossbow" title="Crossbow">crossbows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trebuchet" title="Trebuchet">counterweight trebuchets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannon</a>. The Middle Ages are perhaps best known for their architectural heritage: While the invention of the <a href="/wiki/Rib_vault" title="Rib vault">rib vault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arch" title="Arch">pointed arch</a> gave rise to the high rising <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic style</a>, the ubiquitous medieval fortifications gave the era the almost proverbial title of the 'age of castles'.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Papermaking" title="Papermaking">Papermaking</a>, a 2nd-century Chinese technology, was carried to the Middle East when a group of Chinese papermakers were captured in the 8th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Papermaking technology was spread to Europe by the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">Umayyad conquest of Hispania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> A paper mill was established in Sicily in the 12th century. In Europe the fiber to make pulp for making paper was obtained from linen and cotton rags. Lynn White credited the spinning wheel with increasing the supply of rags, which led to cheap paper, which was a factor in the development of printing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_technology">Renaissance technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Renaissance technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_technology" title="Renaissance technology">Renaissance technology</a></div>
<table style="float:right; border:1px solid darkgrey; background:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td>
<center>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 104px">
<div style="width: 104px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 102px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Filippo_Brunelleschi,_cutaway_of_the_Dome_of_Florence_Cathedral_(Santa_Maria_del_Fiore).JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="542" data-file-width="396" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Filippo_Brunelleschi%2C_cutaway_of_the_Dome_of_Florence_Cathedral_%28Santa_Maria_del_Fiore%29.JPG/153px-Filippo_Brunelleschi%2C_cutaway_of_the_Dome_of_Florence_Cathedral_%28Santa_Maria_del_Fiore%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Filippo_Brunelleschi%2C_cutaway_of_the_Dome_of_Florence_Cathedral_%28Santa_Maria_del_Fiore%29.JPG/230px-Filippo_Brunelleschi%2C_cutaway_of_the_Dome_of_Florence_Cathedral_%28Santa_Maria_del_Fiore%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Filippo_Brunelleschi%2C_cutaway_of_the_Dome_of_Florence_Cathedral_%28Santa_Maria_del_Fiore%29.JPG/307px-Filippo_Brunelleschi%2C_cutaway_of_the_Dome_of_Florence_Cathedral_%28Santa_Maria_del_Fiore%29.JPG 2x" width="102"/></a></div>
</div>

</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162.66666666667px">
<div style="width: 162.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 160.66666666667px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Design_for_a_Flying_Machine.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="508" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Design_for_a_Flying_Machine.jpg/241px-Design_for_a_Flying_Machine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Design_for_a_Flying_Machine.jpg/361px-Design_for_a_Flying_Machine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Design_for_a_Flying_Machine.jpg/482px-Design_for_a_Flying_Machine.jpg 2x" width="161"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">

</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</center>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The era is marked by such profound technical advancements like <a href="/wiki/Perspective_(graphical)" title="Perspective (graphical)">linear perceptivity</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_del_Fiore" title="Santa Maria del Fiore">double shell domes</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bastion_fortress" title="Bastion fortress">Bastion fortresses</a>. Note books of the Renaissance artist-engineers such as <a href="/wiki/Taccola" title="Taccola">Taccola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> give a deep insight into the mechanical technology then known and applied. Architects and engineers were inspired by the structures of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a>, and men like <a href="/wiki/Filippo_Brunelleschi" title="Filippo Brunelleschi">Brunelleschi</a> created the large dome of <a href="/wiki/Florence_Cathedral" title="Florence Cathedral">Florence Cathedral</a> as a result. He was awarded one of the first <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a> ever issued in order to protect an ingenious <a href="/wiki/Crane_(machine)" title="Crane (machine)">crane</a> he designed to raise the large masonry stones to the top of the structure. Military technology developed rapidly with the widespread use of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross-bow" title="Cross-bow">cross-bow</a> and ever more powerful <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a>, as the city-states of Italy were usually in conflict with one another. Powerful families like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medici" title="Medici">Medici</a> were strong patrons of the arts and sciences. <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_in_the_Renaissance" title="History of science in the Renaissance">Renaissance science</a> spawned the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">Scientific Revolution</a>; science and technology began a cycle of mutual advancement.</p>
<p>The invention of the movable cast metal type <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a>, whose pressing mechanism was adapted from an olive screw press, (c. 1441) lead to a tremendous increase in the number of books and the number of titles published.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Age_of_Exploration">Age of Exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Age of Exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" title="Age of Exploration">Age of Exploration</a></div>
<p>An improved sailing ship, the (nau or <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carrack</a>), enabled the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" title="Age of Exploration">Age of Exploration</a> with the <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a>, epitomized by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis_Bacon_(philosopher)" title="Francis Bacon (philosopher)">Francis Bacon</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/New_Atlantis" title="New Atlantis">New Atlantis</a></i>. Pioneers like <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Álvares Cabral">Cabral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Magellan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> explored the world in search of new trade routes for their goods and contacts with Africa, India and China to shorten the journey compared with traditional routes overland. They produced new maps and charts which enabled following mariners to explore further with greater confidence. Navigation was generally difficult, however, owing to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_longitude" title="History of longitude">problem of longitude</a> and the absence of accurate <a href="/wiki/Marine_chronometer" title="Marine chronometer">chronometers</a>. European powers rediscovered the idea of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_code" title="Civil code">civil code</a>, lost since the time of the Ancient Greeks.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_Revolution">Industrial Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_technology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Industrial Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a></div>
<table style="float:right; border:1px solid darkgrey; background:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td>
<center>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 190.66666666667px">
<div style="width: 190.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 188.66666666667px;">
